The current top1 working hypothesis is ICT, with TICT as the current top2 runner-up. ESIPT remains a credible third candidate because the molecule contains phenolic OH and carbonyl-rich motifs that may support proton-transfer preorganization, and neutral aromatic remains a weaker but still credible alternative because the scaffold is highly aromatic and partially rigid. The top1 is only a working hypothesis because the molecule simultaneously contains strong donor/acceptor heterogeneity, extensive aromatic content, and many rotatable substituents, so structural cues alone do not cleanly separate ICT from TICT, nor do they yet exclude ESIPT. Shared prepared structure context is available and ready, which helps bounded microscopic baseline work and later geometry-based macro screening. Macro can realistically provide deterministic local structural screening from exactly one registry-backed capability, such as rotor/torsion topology or H-bond preorganization, but cannot decide the global mechanism by itself. Microscopic can realistically provide one low-cost baseline S0/S1 action on the shared prepared structure, giving indirect electronic/excitation evidence, but it cannot in the first round perform conformer sensitivity, torsion scans, or multistep follow-up workflows. Because both structural and excited-state cues are needed to reduce uncertainty without overcommitting early, the first round should gather both macro and microscopic evidence. The case remains in portfolio screening rather than pairwise contraction because at least one still-credible non-top2 candidate, especially ESIPT, has not yet been directly screened, blocked by capability, or dropped with reason.

### Round 1 | planner | planner_diagnosis

- diagnosis: Top1 is ICT (0.39) and top2 is TICT (0.28). The latest evidence strengthens ICT modestly: macro donor-acceptor layout confirms a heteroatom-rich, conjugated donor-acceptor architecture, and the baseline microscopic bundle is consistent with an electronically soft, charge-transfer-capable system. The same evidence leaves TICT unresolved rather than excluded, because high rotor density and torsional complexity were not directly screened yet. ESIPT remains a still-credible additional hypothesis in coverage debt because phenolic OH/carbonyl motifs are present and no direct preorganization screen has been done. Therefore the case remains legitimately in portfolio screening, not pairwise contraction. The key remaining discriminator now is whether there is structurally plausible intramolecular H-bond/proton-transfer preorganization that would keep ESIPT competitive against ICT/TICT. The best next action is a bounded macro ESIPT screen because it directly reduces high-priority coverage debt with a deterministic registry-backed capability and does so more efficiently than verifier or pairwise work at this stage.

- action: microscopic

- confidence: 0.39

- task_instruction: Current reasoning phase: portfolio_screening. Agent framing mode: portfolio_neutral. Do not treat ICT as settled. Execute exactly one registry-backed macro capability: `screen_intramolecular_hbond_preorganization`. Use the shared prepared structure only. Goal: directly screen the remaining coverage-debt hypothesis ESIPT by reporting whether any phenolic OH/carbonyl or other typed donor/acceptor arrangements show plausible intramolecular H-bond preorganization consistent with ESIPT. Return only bounded structural deliverables supported by this capability: intramolecular H-bond candidate summary, typed donor/acceptor preorganization summary, and local preorganization geometry status. Explicitly note whether the observed geometry makes ESIPT more credible, less credible, or still unresolved.

This is an early-round portfolio case, not a closure-ready pairwise contest.

- final_hypothesis_rationale: null

- capability_assessment: Macro capabilities are well suited for bounded structural screening of alternative mechanisms in this phase. The first microscopic baseline bundle added useful indirect electronic context but, as expected from policy, cannot adjudicate the global mechanism alone. A direct macro screen for ESIPT preorganization is the highest-value next bounded step. Round 1 produced bounded support for ICT-like donor-acceptor behavior from macro donor-acceptor layout screening and a low-gap/allowed-excitation baseline bundle, but portfolio screening is still incomplete because TICT, ESIPT, and neutral aromatic have not yet been directly screened, blocked, or dropped. With 20 rounds remaining including the current context, there is ample budget to resolve coverage debt before pairwise contraction.

### Round 2 | planner | planner_diagnosis

- diagnosis: Top1 is ICT (0.40) and top2 is TICT (0.27). The latest evidence slightly strengthens the current top1 because a second low-gap, allowed-excitation baseline remains compatible with a charge-transfer-capable donor-acceptor system, but it does not directly discriminate ICT from its challengers. The top2 challenger TICT is left essentially unresolved, not weakened decisively, because the molecule still has 17 rotatable bonds, 17 torsion candidates, and heavy branching, yet no dedicated rotor/torsion screening has been run. An additional still-credible hypothesis, ESIPT, remains in coverage debt and is also unresolved because phenolic OH and carbonyl motifs were not directly tested for intramolecular H-bond preorganization. Therefore the case must remain in portfolio screening, not pairwise contraction, since coverage debt is still non-empty. The key remaining discriminator now is whether the structure shows geometry-level preorganization for ESIPT; that is a bounded, direct, registry-backed test. The chosen next action is best now because it directly reduces high-priority coverage debt that the latest round failed to address due to a capability mismatch.

- action: macro

- confidence: 0.4

- task_instruction: Current reasoning phase: portfolio_screening. Agent framing mode: portfolio_neutral. Do not treat ICT as settled. Execute exactly one registry-backed macro capability: `screen_intramolecular_hbond_preorganization`. Use the shared prepared structure only. Screen ESIPT coverage debt directly by reporting: (1) intramolecular H-bond candidate summary, (2) typed donor/acceptor preorganization summary, and (3) local preorganization geometry status. Keep the report bounded to whether geometry-level preorganization exists strongly enough to keep ESIPT credible versus the current ICT-leading portfolio picture. Do not decide the global mechanism.

The analysis must be bounded to structural evidence without making any global mechanism decisions.

The macro capability 'screen_intramolecular_hbond_preorganization' is the best fit for this task and is supported by the runtime environment.
